  1
For U-Plane separate priorities can be supported based on ecpriRtcid / ecpriPcid  (or the equivalent fields in RoE packet 2
headers).  This allows for different prioritization of some channels (e.g. PRACH/ SRS), or services (URLLC).  This 3
requires the ability to configure priority assignments to ecpriRtcid / ecpriPcid via M -Plane messages.   The default U-4
Plane priority can be applied to flows not specifically configured with a different value via the M -Plane.  If a node does 5
not support configurable ecpriRtcid / ecpriPcid priorities, then all U-Plane traffic will use the default value. 6
QoS failure (dropped packets) may be detected using the sequence numbers that make up part of the transport header.  7
Loss of a packet in the U-Plane will generally impact only a specific symbol except in rare cases where a multi -symbol 8
U-Plane message is sent (using the “symInc” field).  Loss of a C-Plane packet is more serious, with the possibility of 9
impacting an entire slot’s worth of data.  A broader impact is also possible with C-Plane packet loss: if downloaded 10
beamforming weights, beamforming attributes, or channel information is lost then a beamId may be incorrectly 11
associated with an “old” set of beamforming weights thereby possibly impacting multiple slots.  However, packet loss 12
can be detected via the sequence number so a recovery action may be taken to re-send messages that may have a 13
persistent impact. 14
3.4 Data Flow Identification 15
Differentiation between U/C-Plane and Management Plane traffic can be achieved using the following options:  16
• Data flow separation based on TCP/UDP (applicable when layer 3 transport is used for the C/U-plane) 17
• Data flow separation based on VLAN (applicable when layer 2 or layer 3 is used for the C/U -plane transport) 18
o Note: The mechanism for assigning VLAN ID to U-Plane and C-Plane is assumed to be via the M-Plane 19
• Data flow separation based on usage of different MAC addresses (applicable when Layer 2 is used for C/U plane 20
transport) 21
o e.g., separate MAC address used for M-Plane and U-Plane, or for baseband load sharing purposes 22
• Data flow separation based on different EtherTypes (applicable when Layer 2 is used for C/U plane transport) 23
The U-plane application also needs to uniquely associate different data flows (e.g. spatial streams) each with a 24
unique U/C plane endpoint address. This can be achieved un an O-RU using the eAxC identifier, and in the O-DU 25
using the eAxC identifier in combination with transport-based endpoint identifiers to differentiate O-RUs. In 26
addition, O-RU data flows can be switched/routed to different O-DUs (or different O-DU ports or O-DU 27
processors) according to the transport-based identifiers associated with an eAxCid (referred to as processing -28
elements in the WG4 M-Plane Specification) to allow frames/packets to be switched/routed by network equipment 29
with no visibility of the eAxC values carried in the eCPRI/1914.3 header.  30
 Different transport identifiers (e.g. UDP/IP, VLAN, MAC) can be used based on whether layer 2 or layer 3 transport is 31
used for the U/C plane: 32
• U/C-plane data flow separation using UDP-port identifiers (applicable when layer 3 transport is used for the C/U -33
plane) 34
• U/C-plane data flow separation using on VLAN identities (applicable when layer 2 or layer 3 is used for the C/U -35
plane transport) 36
• U/C-plane data flow separation based on usage of different MAC addresses (applicable when Layer 2 is used for 37
C/U plane transport) 38
 39

3.5 Fragmentation 1
Fragmentation is applied in case data (U-Plane or C-Plane data) with Ethernet transport overheads to be transferred 2
exceed maximum transmission unit (MTU) of the network. This specification allows two methods for fragmentation, 3
application layer fragmentation and transport layer fragmentation: 4
3.5.1 Application layer fragmentation 5
• Application creates C-plane or U-Plane messages, which when including overheads can fit to MTU 6
requirements set by network 7
• Sequence ID: Sequence ID increases for every message, E=1, Subsequence ID=0  8
An example of application fragmentation is provided in Figure 3-10, wherein a long data section is split between 9
multiple U-Plane messages.  In the example it is a single data section (0xABC) so described as such in the C -Plane, and 10
in the U-Plane the sectionId is cited multiple times in the multiple U-Plane messages but with differing and consecutive 11
groups of PRBs as indicated by the startPrbu and numPrbu fields.  The I and Q word width in the example is 14 bits, 12
which for such a large data section requires multiple U-Plane messages.  The ecpriRtcid / ecpriPcid (0xDEF3) is shown 13
with a random example value, as is the sequence ID in the C-Plane (0x99) and independently in the U-Plane (0x40-14
0x48). 15
 16
 17
Figure 3-10 : Example of Application-Level Fragmentation of U-Plane Messages 18
 19
3.5.2 Radio Transport layer (eCPRI or IEEE-1914.3) fragmentation 20
o Application creates U-Plane messages, which when including overhead may exceed MTU 21
requirements set by network 22
o Radio transport layer splits message which may contain more than one section into pieces such that 23
the fragments with overheads fit to MTU requirements set by network. 24
o Sequence ID: Sequence ID remains same for all the fragments. Subsequence ID starts from 0 for the 25
first fragment and counts up for each fragment. Last fragment flagged with E=1, othe rs E=0. 26
 27

3.5.3 Fragmentation Guideline 2
Application layer fragmentation should be applied so that maximum size standard IEEE 802.3 Ethernet frames can be 3
used. (Jumbo frames, if used, increase the maximum MTU size). 4
• In case of L2 only solution, application layer maximum transmission unit size is  standard IEEE 802.3 Ethernet 5
frame payload size (1500 bytes) – transport overhead (8 bytes) = 1492 bytes (or larger for Jumbo frames) 6
When a U-plane section payload is fragmented due to large number of PRBs, it will be divided into multiple groups of 7
PRBs such that each group (including the application headers) can fit to the MTU requirements. Each group of PRBs 8
shall have its respective control fields including the same section ID from the C-plane and startPrbu and numPrbu to 9
identify its contents (See Figure 3-9).  When an application layer message exceeds the MTU size set via the M-Plane 10
configuration, radio-transport layer fragmentation can be applied at the transport layer and has the advantage of 11
allowing application layer messages to fit whatever is the MTU size without the application having to know about 12
transport-level details.  13
  14

Chapter 5 C-plane Protocol 1
5.1 General 2
5.2 Function 3
5.2.1 C-Plane Transport 4
Either eCPRI or IEEE 1914.3 is used as an encapsulation mechanism for the control-plane messages. Due to the nature 5
of these messages (very strict delay constraints), it is assumed that message acknowledgements are not possible . 6
Likewise, it is assumed that a different data flow is used other than the U-Plane channel. Further, C-Plane messages are 7
not concatenated with U-Plane messages within same Ethernet frame. 8
5.3 Elementary Procedures 9
5.3.1 Scheduling and Beamforming Commands Transfer procedure 10
This procedure is used to exchange C-Plane messages between O-DU and O-RU. The main purpose of these messages 11
is to transmit data-associated control information required for processing of user data (e.g., scheduling  and 12
beamforming commands). Messages are sent separately for DL related commands and UL related commands (see 13
Figure 5-1).  See also Figure 5-7 for the special case of LTE LAA wherein there are UL as well as DL C-Plane 14
message flows.  For purpose of increased flexibility, C-Plane messages may be sent either jointly or separately 15
depending on the channel for which information is conveyed. For example, PUCCH and PUSCH may be bundled or not 16
bundled into a single C-Plane message depending on implementation.  17

5.3.2 Mixed Numerology and PRACH Handling 1
5G NR defines Physical Resource Block (PRB) where the number of subcarriers per PRB is the same for all 2
numerologies (twelve). However, subcarrier spacing may differ, resulting in mixed numerology used in time and 3
frequency domains respectively. Likewise, mixed numerologies may be applied to both DL and UL respectively 4
(Figure 5-2). 5
 6
Figure 5-2 : Mixed Numerology in Time and Frequency Domain 7
Frequency indexing across multiple numerologies  8
• RB indexing (i.e. the physical resource block) is always dependent on the used numerology. For PRACH and 9
SSB the relation is with the physical channel. In case of PRACH, indexing of RBs inside of each PRACH 10
frequency block follows 3GPP specifications and PRACH subcarrier extraction is performed in the O-DU. In 11
particular, the first RE of the first RB addressed inside section Id shall corresponds with the first guard tone 12
used at the lower edge of the PRACH block frequency block and based on the PRACH SCS. The O-RU, using 13
the filter index knows the PRACH subcarrier position and guard tones and can then adjust its filtering 14
parameters (e.g. filter center, passband). For the SSB case, its own separate frequency offset is assigned.  15
• For each numerology (and PRACH/SSB), the freqOffset IE defines the relative spacing between the center of 16
RE#0 of RB#0 to the component carrier center (i.e. equivalently DC=0Hz when normalized with regard to the 17
component carrier center), and using resolution of half the SCS of the respective numerology. This concept is 18
depicted in Figure 5-3, Figure 5-4 and Figure 5-5. 19
o The component carrier center (RF frequency in Hz) is the common reference to all numerologies and 20
PRACH/SSB channels. Further, the relation between DC=0Hz of the carrier and ARFCN (RF 21
frequency in Hz of the carrier center) is to be defined at carrier setup over M -Plane. 22
o Spacing resolution of 0.5 x SCS allows DC to be aligned with an RE center, or and RE edge.  23
 24
 25
 26
Figure 5-3 : RB Mapping– PRACH Example 27
 28

Slot indexing with mixed numerologies 7
For a given frequency range FR1 or FR2, the highest possible numerology supported by the O-RU shall be used as the 8
common reference per component carrier for the start of the slot identified by slotId.  UL and DL on the same 9
component carrier shall use the same reference numerology for slotId.  If the highest numerology supported by the O-10
RU allows both normal and extended CP then normal CP shall be used as reference. Note that the O-RU shall advance 11
slots with extended CP against the reference.  The symbol duration and position in time is calculated from the µ value 12
(SCS from frameStruture in message field or configured via M-plane) and the slotId field in the CU-Plane message.   13
The value of the sectionId field in CU-Plane messages addressed per eAxC shall be unique per slot identified by slotId 14
value. 15
For example, in FR1 case, the maximum slot numbers per subframe is four, since the maximum SCS is 60kHz  16
• µ= 0 → slot #0; µ=1 → slot #0 & #2; µ=2 → slot #0, #1, #2, #3 (see Table 5-1) 17

PRACH formats with multiple repetitions of preamble 5
Certain PRACH formats lead to PRACH symbols to be constructed from multiple repet itions of a preamble sequence, 6
with only the Cyclic Prefix (CP) used with the first sequence. Therefore, the O-RU must be informed how to correctly 7
execute CP extraction and FFT.  Based on implementation, this may e.g. be achieved by sending each repetition inside a 8
PRACH occasion as a separate symbol (in a separate message and separate Section ID) , or by sending a single control 9
message spanning over multiple symbols (e.g. example depicted in Figure 5-6: number of symbols = 4, CP length = 0, 10
time offset duration is adjusted by an equivalent time value of 1152 samples to compensate for setting CP length =0 ), 11
which reduces the number of C-Plane messages and data sections required.  12
Optionally O-RU can advertise the list of the supported formats for the specific endpoint. If the O-RU chooses not to, it 13
means O-RU supports all PRACH formats and the O-DU may select whatever format that is 3GPP compliant with the 14
selected SCS. If the O-RU implements earlier releases of the M-plane specification which does not support such 15
reporting, then the negotiation of PRACH formats to use must happen offline, i.e. operators and/or vendors have to 16
ensure that the intended PRACH formats are supported by both O-RU and O-DU. 17

5.3.4 LAA Commands Transfer procedure 1
This procedure is used to exchange C-Plane messages between O-DU and O-RU. The main purpose of these messages 2
is to support LAA feature in the O-RU/O-DU.  See Annex G for more details on the LAA message flow. 3
5.3.4.1 LBT procedure overview  4
The LBT procedure is used to configure the O-RU with the parameters needed to do LBT prior to PDSCH or DRS 5
transmission OTA. The O-RU needs to report the LBT process outcome (either success or failure) in the indication 6
message.  7
In contrast to licensed spectrum, where the O-RU may continuously send data or reference signals OTA, in unlicensed 8
spectrum, the O-RU can only send discontinuous bursts of data (of length MCOT) or periodic DRS signals. The 9
LBT_DL_CONFIG request message is sent once prior to each OTA transmission on the LAA SCell. This includes both 10
DRS and PDSCH (i.e., MCOT burst) transmissions. For every LBT_DL_CONFIG  request message, the O-RU replies 11
with the LBT_DL indication messages which include the LBT outcome and the status of the subframe 12
(transmitted/dropped) (see Figure 5-7). 13
If O-RU can manage a congestion window by itself, the O-DU does not need to send LBT_DL_CONFIG request 14
message to start the LBT procedure at O-RU. Because O-RU can determine the start timing of LBT procedure, the 15
requirements of O-DU for the LBT procedure at the O-RU is a delivery of needed information to adjust a congestion 16
window managed by O-RU. To transmit these information, O-DU sends LBT_CWCONFIG_REQ message, and O-RU 17
notifies to the O-DU by LBT_CWCONFIG_RSP message to indicate that the LBT_CWCONFIG_REQ message is 18
successfully received or not. Also, O-RU can adjust its congestion window based on the information on the 19
LBT_CWCONFIG_REQ message.  For every LBT_CWCONFIG_REQ request message, the O-RU replies with the 20
LBT_DL indication message(s) which include the LBT outcome and the status of the subframe (transm itted/dropped). 21
For the DRS signal, initially, the O-DU must configure the O-RU with the DRS parameters (DMTC period and DMTC 22
offset) via the M-plane. 23
Before every DRS period, the O-DU must send the LBT_DL_CONFIG request message and the DRS signal. O-RU 24
does LBT and transmits the DRS signal OTA in case of LBT success. The O-RU then must send the LBT_DL 25
indication. 26
The DRS signal can be transmitted over the fronthaul interface similar to other reference signals such  as the 27
PSS/SSS/CRS.  28

5.3.4.2 Definitions 5
• 𝐷𝑂𝑊: Maximum one-way fronthaul latency 6
• 𝑃𝐷𝑈: Maximum O-DU processing time (reading an upstream O-RU c-plane message, MAC processing, 7
sending the downstream U-plane data) 8
• 𝑃𝑅𝑈: Maximum O-RU processing time (sending an upstream c-plane message, receiving downstream U-plane 9
data, transmitting U-plane data OTA)  10
• 𝐵𝑅𝑈: O-RU Buffer depth (for LAA) ceiled to an integer number of OFDM symbols in microseconds (up to 140 11
symbols, for example (i.e., MCOT)). This is equivalent to the minimum amount of data that must be buffered 12
at the O-RU. This parameter could be less than or equal to the actual O-RU buffer size communicated via the 13
M-Plane.  14
• Expired symbol: Symbol where the current time at the O-RU exceeds its target transmission time (i.e., 15
SFN/SF) OTA.  16
• Normal (partially-filled) SF assumption: 𝑇𝑠𝑡𝑎𝑟𝑡 is the start of the transmission time, which occurs at the first SF 17
(slot) boundary the O-RU encounters after starting the LBT CAT 4 process and after finishing the minimum 18
sensing duration. Initially known to the O-DU (since it sends the LBT start time and the LBT parameters to the 19
O-RU). It can be updated in real-time based on the LBT outcome and the communication between the O-DU 20
and O-RU.  Note that here, a “slot” follows the LTE definition of containing seven symbols.  21

5.3.4.3 General Guidelines for the LAA-procedure 10
5.3.4.3.1 PDSCH Transmission 11
• O-DU should avoid buffer overflow or underflow at the O-RU: 12
• O-DU should only send 𝐵𝑅𝑈 worth of data to the O-RU for every single transmission 13
• O-DU should plan for the data to be received at the O-RU only 𝑃𝑅𝑈 before the actual OTA 14
transmission time at the O-RU 15
• O-RU should avoid buffer overflow or underflow at the O-RU: 16
• O-RU should flush its buffer (by dropping any expired symbols) as soon as any symbol becomes 17
expired (i.e., current time is larger than the symbol’s scheduled time) 18
• O-RU should immediately send a success LBT indication to the O-DU once the channel is acquired.  19
• The O-RU should send an error message to the O-DU if data received is larger than its local buffer  20
• The O-RU should send an subframe drop or transmission message to the O-DU when buffered 21
subframe is dropped because scheduled time is passed, or is transmitted after LBT success.  22
• The O-RU should have a buffer that satisfies the following equation: 𝐵𝑅𝑈 ≥2×𝐷𝑂𝑊 +𝑃𝐷𝑈 +𝑃𝑅𝑈 23
• Note on LBT CAT 4 in general: 24
• The O-DU can configure the O-RU (via the M-plane) with the threshold on the LBT CAT 4 duration 25
(e.g., 8 ms). Once this threshold has exceeded, the O-RU sends a failure LBT indication to the O-DU, 26

• DRS signal is sent every SF in the 6 SFs of the DRS window until LBT succeeds .  15

For the NR case, data symbol numbering in a slot shall be from zero to thirteen (for extended CP, eleven).  For LTE the 33
symbol numbering shall be mapped to the NR numbering as follows: 34
LTE with normal prefix maps to NR with same μ and normal prefix: 35
 LTE symbol 𝑙𝐿𝑇𝐸 of slot 2𝑖 is mapped to NR slot 𝑖, symbol 𝑙′=𝑙𝐿𝑇𝐸 36
 LTE symbol 𝑙𝐿𝑇𝐸 of slot 2𝑖+1 is mapped to NR slot 𝑖, symbol 𝑙′ =7+𝑙𝐿𝑇𝐸 37
LTE with extended prefix the following applies: 38
 LTE symbol 𝑙𝐿𝑇𝐸 of slot 2𝑖 is mapped to NR slot 𝑖, symbol 𝑙′=𝑙𝐿𝑇𝐸 39
 LTE symbol 𝑙𝐿𝑇𝐸 of slot 2𝑖+1 is mapped to NR slot 𝑖, symbol 𝑙′ =6+𝑙𝐿𝑇𝐸 40

5.3.6 Dynamic Spectrum Sharing (DSS) 1
Dynamic Spectrum sharing allows different technologies – 4G LTE and 5G NR in this version of the specification, to 2
share same frequency carrier dynamically, i.e. the O-DU may allocate one or more set(s) of frequency-time resources 3
(or PRBs) to LTE or NR dynamically. The O-RU also must support this feature for the O-DU to take advantage of such 4
an allocation. This version of the specification supports DSS via using dedicated eAxC ids (i.e. endpoints) for LTE and 5
NR or via using Section Extension =9 for DSS. 6
5.3.6.1 Dynamic Spectrum Sharing (DSS) via Dedicated Endpoints 7
Dedicated endpoints are configured in the O-RU for LTE and NR (hence dedicated eAxC ids) to implement DSS. For 8
e.g. when an O-DU allocates a set of PRBs for LTE, O-DU uses an eAxC id dedicated for LTE (assigned to a carrier 9
identified as an LTE carrier) to address the LTE endpoint; at a different time when the O -DU allocates the same set of 10
PRBs for NR, the O-DU uses eAxC id dedicated for NR (assigned to a carrier identified as an NR carrier) to address the 11
NR endpoint in the O-RU.  12
When using this approach, a carrier will be assigned to LTE or NR, so when both LTE and NR are to be s upported at 13
the same time (“DSS”), two carriers with overlapping frequency ranges are to be identified, one being LTE and the 14
other being NR.  It will be up to the O-RU to overlap the two carriers such that the same frequency range can support 15
both NR and LTE, and it will be up to the O-DU to assure that no RE is assigned to both LTE and NR at the same time. 16
5.3.6.2 Dynamic Spectrum Sharing (DSS) via Section Extension =9 for DSS 17
Using Section Extension =9 for DSS, the O-DU can use a single eAxC id (and hence a single endpoint) for conveying 18
LTE and NR PRB allocations if the O-RU is capable of handling both LTE and NR processing using one endpoint (i.e. 19
the O-RU indicates support for Section Extension =9). Note that a single carrier may be allocated to either LTE, NR or 20
both, and supporting DSS in this manner means the carrier (to which the endpoint is assigned) would be designated as 21
supporting both.  The O-DU indicates whether the PRB allocation information is applicable to LTE or to NR via 22
Section Extension =9.   23
 24
5.4 Elements for the C-plane Protocol 25
5.4.1 General 26
C-Plane messages are encapsulated using a two-layered header approach. The first layer consists of a eCPRI common 27
header or IEEE 1914.3 common header, including corresponding fields used to indicate the message type, while the 28
second layer is an application layer including necessary fields for control and synchronization.  Within the application 29
layer, a “section” defines the characteristics of U-plane data to be transferred or received from a beam with one pattern 30
id.  In general, the transmission header, application header, and sections are all intended to be aligned on 4 -byte 31
boundaries and are transmitted in “network byte order” meaning the most significant byte of a multi-byte parameter is 32
transmitted first. 33
When the optional “little endian byte order” is chosen via M-plane, the beamforming weights (Section Type 1 or 3, and 34
extType = 1) and ciIsample/ciQsample (Section Type 6) fields shall use little endian byte order to transmit the complex 35
numbers. Annex D.1 shows little endian byte order format for various I/Q data length.  36
 37
Table 5-2 described the section types are supported within the C-Plane. 38
 39
Table 5-2 : Section Types 40
Section
Type
Target Scenario Remarks
0 Unused Resource Blocks or
symbols in Downlink or Uplink
Indicates to O-RU that certain Resource Blocks or symbols will not be
used (idle periods, guard periods). Likewise, there are no associated
U-Plane messages containing IQ data for this Section Type.

during the specified idle interval for e.g. power-savings or to provide
an interval for calibration.

5.4.1.1 Section Extensions 2
Within a data section the section header in most cases includes a “extension flag” which indicates parameters that apply 3
to the section beyond those within the section header (the extension flag is most often adjacent to the beamId or ueId 4
fields).  The presence of this extension flag indicates that following the header a section extension is present.  Within 5
the section extension is another extension flag, adjacent to the “extType” field, which indicates that a second (or third, 6
etc.) extension is present.  In this way any number of section extensions may be included within a data section.  This 7
provides an extensibility for section parameters without the need to continually redefine the section header or create 8
new section types to accommodate future fronthaul specification needs. 9
The section extension takes the form reminiscent of “TLV”: there is a type field specifically “extType” which is a 7 -bit 10
field describing the specific extension type, then a one-byte length field specifically “extLen” field detailing how many 11
4-byte words are contained in the extension (minimum of 1 including the “extType” and “extLen” fields), and then 12
some number of parameters that depend on the “extType” value for their definition.  In all cases the section extension 13
will be an integer number of (4-byte) words in length. 14
Specific valid values of “extType”, their meanings and their associated parameters are detailed in subsequent sub-15
chapters of this spec.  16
 17
5.4.2 Scheduling and Beamforming Commands  18
A common frame format is used for C-Plane messages, consisting of a transport layer and an application layer. The 19
application layer is within the transport layer payload and consists of a common header for time reference, followed by 20
information and parameters dependent and specific to the Section Type in use. Multiple sets of section data of the same 21
Section Type value can be lined up one after another within the payload. To minimize packet rate over the interface, 22
transmitter should fill messages with as many subsequent sections (with or without sequential section IDs) as possible. 23
However, sets of section data of different Section Type values are to be sent via separate messages (i.e. different values 24
of Section Type shall not be mixed within a single C-Plane message payload). 25
 26
o Transport Layer (see section 3.1.3) 27
o Application Layer 28
o Section Type “0” Fields (used for indicating idle or guard periods from O-DU to O-RU) 29

• dataDirection (data direction (gNB Tx/Rx)) field: 1 bit  31
• payloadVersion (payload version) field: 3 bits 32
• value = “1” shall be set (1st protocol version for payload and time reference format)  33

5.4.3 Coding of Information Elements – Transport Layer 4
See Section 3.1.3 for transport header information element details. 5
5.4.4 Coding of Information Elements – Application Layer, Common 6
5.4.4.1 dataDirection (data direction (gNB Tx/Rx)) 7
Description: This parameter indicates the gNB data direction.  8
Value range: {0b=Rx (i.e. UL), 1b=Tx (i.e. DL)}. 9
Type: binary bit. 10
Field length: 1 bit. 11
 12
5.4.4.2 payloadVersion (payload version) 13
Description: This parameter defines the payload protocol version valid for the following IEs in the application layer. In 14
this version of the specification payloadVersion=001b shall be used.  15
Value range: {000b-111b=Payload version}. 16
Type: unsigned integer. 17
Field length: 3 bits. 18
Default Value: 001b (version 1 assumed). 19
 20
5.4.4.3 filterIndex (filter index) 21
Description: This parameter defines an index to the channel filter to be used between IQ data and air interface, both in 22
DL and UL. For most physical channels filterIndex =0000b is used which indexes the standard channel filter, e.g. 23
100MHz channel filter for 100MHz nominal carrier bandwidth. Another use case is PRACH in UL, where different 24
filter indices can be used for different PRACH formats, assuming that before FFT processing of PRACH data there is a 25

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2020 by the O-RAN Alliance.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        76
O-RAN.WG4.CUS.0-v03.00
separate PRACH filter or PRACH filter in addition to the standard channel filter in UL. Please note that for PRACH 1

filter index = 0000b is also allowed for PRACH. 4

first fragmented section. 8

5.4.4.10 udCompHdr (user data compression header) 30
See section 6.3.3.13 for the description of this parameter. 31
The udCompHdr information is provided on the U-Plane, instructing the O-RU (on DL) and O-DU (on UL) how to 32
interpret and decompress the received U-Plane data.  However, the O-RU is not expected to decide by itself the best UL 33
data format and data compression method, instead the O-DU shall instruct the O-RU via udCompHdr in a C-Plane 34
message.  This means the udCompHdr in a C-Plane message only has meaning for UL U-Plane data (dataDirection = 35
0b) and should be set to 0x00 when dataDirection = 1b (DL data), and the receiving O-RU shall ignore the received 36
udCompHdr value.  When static data format and compression is used (see 6.1.2) then udCompHdr is not needed in any 37
C-Plane message and should be set to 0x00, and the receiving O-RU shall ignore the received udCompHdr value. 38
Note that it is impermissible to specify different values of udCompHdr for the same data section, even if discriminated 39
by different reMask values.  Only a single compression method per data section is supported.   The O-RU response if 40
the C-Plane specifies multiple udCompHdr values for a single data section is undefined.  41
 42

O-RAN.WG4.CUS.0-v03.00

5.4.4.12 timeOffset (time offset) 9
Description: This parameter defines the time_offset from the start of the slot to the start of the Cyclic Prefix (CP) in 10
number of samples Ts (=1/30.72MHz as specified in 3GPP TS38.211 section 4.1).  The value shall be less than the 11
baseline slot length used for slot ID counting as defined in section 5.3.2. 12
time_offset = timeOffset * ts 13
Value range: {0000 0000 0000 0000b-1111 1111 1111 1111b}. 14
Type: unsigned integer. 15
Field length: 16 bits. 16

per 1ms sub-frame according to 3GPP TS 38.211, taking for completeness also 3GPP TS 36.211 into account. The 21
parameter µ=0…5 from 3GPP TS 38.211 is extended to apply for PRACH processing.  22
NOTE: The parameter “FFTSize” is meant to facilitate the above calculation and is not meant t o strictly dictate the O-23
RU’s method of time-to-frequency conversion. 24

5.4.4.14 cpLength (cyclic prefix length) 6
Description: This parameter defines the length CP_length of the Cyclic Prefix (CP) as follows, based on T s 7
(=1/30.72MHz as specified in 3GPP TS38.211 section 4.1): 8
CP_length = cpLength * Ts  9

plane message. In addition to the values defined in 3GPP, the value 0 is supported. The slot start time reference 11
differentiation between normal CP and extended CP is based on cpLength and frameStructure. If cpLength is zero then 12
differentiation between normal CP and extended CP time reference is based on cp -type parameter conveyed in the M-13
Plane.  With section type 1, the CP properties shall be configured over M-Plane. In the latter case, the cyclic prefix shall 14
have the following properties: 15
- cp-type: Normal or extended 16
- cp-length: same unit as cpLength defined in this section; used for symbol 0 for NR & LTE, and symbol 7*2µ for NR 17
(µ as defined in the table above with “NA” for µ shall be replaced by “0”)  18
- cp-length-other: same unit as cpLength defined in this section; used for other symbols than by cp -length 19

5.4.5 Coding of Information Elements – Application Layer, Sections 24
5.4.5.1 sectionId (section identifier) 25
Description: This parameter identifies individual data sections described within the C-Plane message. The purpose of 26
the section ID is to map U-Plane data sections to the corresponding C-Plane message (and Section Type) associated 27
with the data.  Two or more C-Plane data section descriptions with same Section ID may be cited corresponding to a 28
single U-Plane data section containing a combined payload for both citations (e.g., for supporting mixed CSI RS and 29
PDSCH). This case is applicable when usage of reMask is complimentary (or orthogonal) and different beam directions 30
(i.e. beamIds) are given the resource elements.  Data sections are specific to a value of eAxC so different eAxC values 31
may have differently-defined data sections e.g. have different ranges of PRBs contained within.  32
NOTES:  33

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2020 by the O-RAN Alliance.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        80
O-RAN.WG4.CUS.0-v03.00
▪ In the case of two section descriptions with same Section ID, both sections shall have same rb, startPrbc, 1
numPrbc, udCompHdr, and numSymbol IE fields’ content.  2
▪ An upper bound on the max number of section IDs that can be addressed per eAxC or per sets of eAxCs, per 3
symbol and per slot, for DL and for UL respectively, shall be conveyed via M-plane messaging as part of the 4
O-RU capabilities description. 5
▪ sectionIds are specific to a slot, so sectionId values may be “reused” for each slot, and the sectionId value for 6
one slot has no specified relation to the sectionId value for a different slot. 7
▪ The sectionId cited in a C-Plane message must have the same value as the sectionId in the corresponding U -8
Plane message for the given data section as defined by the frameId, subFrameId, slotId, startSymbolid fields 9
and range of relevant PRBs as indicated by the totality of the specified startPrb(c/u) and numPrb(c/u) fields. 10
Value range: {0000 0000 0000b-1111 1111 1111b}. 11
Type: unsigned integer. 12
Field length: 12 bits. 13
 14
5.4.5.2 rb (resource block indicator) 15
Description: This parameter is used to indicate if every RB is used or every other RB is used. The starting RB is 16
defined by startPrbc and total number of used RBs is defined by numPrbc.  Example: RB=1, startPrb=1, numPrb=3, 17
then the PRBs used are 1, 3, and 5.  If numPrbc=0 (i.e., all PRBs), then the sending node shall set the rb value to zero, 18
and the receiving node shall ignore whatever rb value is received and assume it is zero.  19
Value range: {0b=every RB used; 1b=every other RB used}. 20
Type: binary bit. 21
Field length: 1 bit. 22
Default Value: 0b (every RB used). 23
 24
5.4.5.3 symInc (symbol number increment command) 25
Description: This parameter is used to indicate which symbol number is relevant to the given sectionId.  It is expected 26
that for each C-Plane message a symbol number is maintained and starts with the value of startSymbolid.  The same 27
value is used for each section in the message as long as symInc is zero.  When symInc is one, the maintained symbol 28
number should be incremented to the next symbol, and that new symbol number should be used for that section and 29
each subsequent section until the symInc bit is again detected to be one.  In the case of a multiple-symbol data section 30
(numSymbol > 1), the new symbol number shall be the one after the last symbol in the data section.  In this manner, 31
multiple symbols may be handled by a single C-Plane message.   32
A few other points regarding use of symInc in the C-Plane: 33
a) SymInc may be used when different data sections have a different number of symbols under certain conditions 34
namely that the data section descriptions in the C-Plane message are carefully arranged.  The arrangement 35
must be such that the following procedure as applied by the O-RU works correctly: 36
symbol[s] - symbol addressed by section description s=1…N (considers section descriptions in one C -37
Plane message, s=1 identifies the first section description) shall be calculated as follows: 38
Let symInc[s] and numSymbols[s] are values of corresponding fields of section description s  39
For sake of simplicity let symbol[0] = startSymbolId, symInc[0]=0 and numSymbols[0]=1  40
for s=1…N (all section descriptions in a message) 41
If symInc[s] = 0 then symbol[s] = symbol[s-1]  42
Else symbol[s] = symbol[s-1] + numSymbols[s-1] 43
b) When a data section description is cited multiple times (e.g. with different reMask values) if the value of 44
symInc is to be set to 1, then only the first invocation of the sectionID shall have symInc=1 and all other 45
invocations of the sectionId shall have symInc=0 in the same C-Plane message.  This assures that the above 46

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2020 by the O-RAN Alliance.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        81
O-RAN.WG4.CUS.0-v03.00
rule can be applied (in the same C-Plane message only) while assuring that all invocations of the data section 1
descriptions will refer to the same symbols, which must be the case whether the invocations are in the same C -2
Plane message or in separate C-Plane messages. 3
Use of symInc in the U-Plane is independent of the use of symInc in the C-Plane. The current view is that U-Plane 4
message includes data for a single symbol (to avoid degrading the latency performance of the U -Plane), so use of 5
symInc=1 is prohibited in the U-Plane as of this version of the specification. A future version may allow use of  6
symInc=1 in the U-Plane to allow multiple symbols to be contained in a single U-Plane message.  7
 8
Value range: {0b=use the current symbol number; 1b=increment the current symbol number and use that}.  9
Type: binary bit. 10
Field length: 1 bit. 11
Default Value: 0b (do not increment the current symbol number). 12
 13
5.4.5.4 startPrbc (starting PRB of data section description) 14
Description: This parameter is the starting PRB of a data section described in the C-Plane message.  Values of 15
startPrbc and numPrbc must ensure that data sections must never overlap: a single PRB may only exist within one data 16
section for a given value of eAxC.  For one C-Plane message, there may be multiple U-Plane messages associated with 17
it and requiring defining from which PRB the control commands are applicable.  18
Note: freqOffset affects the frequency span for specific range of PRB numbers. Therefore "must never overlap" must 19
consider the value of freqOffset. 20
Value range: {00 0000 0000b-11 1111 1111b}. 21
Type: unsigned integer. 22
Field length: 10 bits. 23
 24
5.4.5.5 reMask (resource element mask) 25
Description: This parameter defines the Resource Element (RE) mask within an PRB. Each bit setting in the reMask 26
indicates if the section control is applicable to the RE sent in U-Plane messages (0=not applicable; 1=applicable).  MSB 27
indicates the value for the RE of the lowest frequency in a PRB. 28
Note that different REs in a PRB may be indicated by different invocations of the same section Id but with differing 29
reMasks; the maximum number of different reMask values that may be applied to a PRB is an O-RU characteristic that 30
is conveyed from the O-RU to the O-DU via the M-Plane.  If any RE in a PRB is never pointed to by an reMask (but 31
other REs in that PRB are), the “missing” RE should be set to zero in the U-Plane, and no beamforming ID or other 32
processing should be applied to the “missing” RE.  No RE may be referenced more than once in a data section. 33
Value range: {0000 0000 0000b-1111 1111 1111b}. 34
Type: unsigned integer (bit mask). 35
Field length: 12 bits. 36
Default Value: 1111 1111 1111b (all REs in the block applicable). 37
 38
5.4.5.6 numPrbc (number of contiguous PRBs per data section description) 39
Description: This parameter defines the PRBs within the data section being described. Values of startPrbc and 40
numPrbc must ensure that data sections must never overlap: a single PRB may only exist within one data section for a 41
given value of eAxC.   42
Value range: {0000 0001b-1111 1111b, 0000 0000b = all PRBs}. 43

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2020 by the O-RAN Alliance.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        82
O-RAN.WG4.CUS.0-v03.00
 Value 0000 0000b is particularly relevant for NR cases wherein the total number of PRBs may be more than 255.  In 1
this case, the sending node shall set the startPrbc value to zero and the receiving node shall ignore whatever startPrbc 2
value is received and assume it is zero. 3
Type: unsigned integer. 4
Field length: 8 bits. 5
 6
5.4.5.7 numSymbol (number of symbols) 7
Description: This parameter defines number of symbols to which the section control is applicable. At minimum, the 8
section control shall be applicable to at least one symbol. However, possible optimizations could allow for several (up 9
to 14) symbols, if e.g., all 14 symbols use the same beam ID. 10
Value range: {0001b-1110b=number of symbols, 0000b=reserved, 1111b=reserved}. 11
Type: unsigned integer. 12
Field length: 4 bits. 13

5.4.5.8 ef (extension flag) 15
Description: This parameter is used to indicate if this section has any Section Extensions as described in section 5.4.6 16

5.4.5.9 beamId (beam identifier) 23
Description: This parameter defines the beam pattern to be applied to the U-Plane data. beamId = 0 means no 24
beamforming operation will be performed. 25
Note that the beamId encodes the beamforming to be done on the O-RU.  This beamforming may be digital, analog or 26
both (“hybrid beamforming”) and the beamId provides all the information necessary for the O-RU to select the correct 27
beam (or weight table or beam attributes from which to create a beam).  It is intended that the beamId be global for the 28
O-RU meaning there are 32767 possible beams shared within the O-RU for all Rtcids/Pcids and shared between UL and 29
DL (beamId=0x0000 is reserved for no beamforming).  The specific mapping of beamId to e.g. weight table, beam 30
attributes, directionality, beam adjacency or any other beam designator is specific to the O-RU design and must be 31
conveyed via M-Plane from the O-RU to O-DU upon startup. 32
NOTE: An upper bound on the max number of beamIDs that can be addressed per eAxC or per sets of eAxCs, per 33
symbol and per slot, for DL and for UL respectively, shall be conveyed via  M-plane messaging as part of the O-RU 34
capabilities description. 35
Value range: {000 0000 0000 0001b-111 1111 1111 1111b; 000 0000 0000 0000b means no BF to be done} 36
Type: unsigned integer. 37
Field length: 15 bits. 38
Default Value: 0000 0000 0000 0000b (no beamforming). 39
 40

O-RAN.WG4.CUS.0-v03.00

5.4.5.11 freqOffset (frequency offset) 9
Description: This parameter defines the frequency offset with respect to the carrier center frequency before additional 10
filtering (e.g. for PRACH) and FFT processing (in UL) in steps of one half the subcarrier spacings f. The frequency 11
offset shall be individual per data section (one cannot use reMask to allow different frequency offsets for different REs 12
in the PRBs). 13
 frequency_offset = freqOffset * f * 0.5 14
Note: Frequency span resulting from frameStructure, freqOffset, startPrbc, numPrbc, and rb must not exceed channel 15
bandwidth configured for eAxC over M-plane. 16
Value range: { 0x000000=no offset,  17
0x000001 – 0x7FFFFF = positive frequency offset,  18
0x800000 – 0xFFFFFF = negative frequency offset }. 19
Type: signed integer. 20
Field length: 24 bits. 21

5.4.5.12 regularizationFactor (regularization Factor) 23
Description: This parameter provides a signed value to support MMSE operation within the O-RU when beamforming 24
weights are supported in the O-RU, so related to section type 6. 25
Value range: {0000 0000 0000 0000b-1111 1111 1111 1111b} 26
Type: unsigned integer. 27

5.4.5.13 ciIsample, ciQsample (channel information I and Q values) 30
Description: These values are the channel information complex values relayed from the O-DU to the O-RU, related to 31
section type 6.  The order of transmission is first Prbc for the first antenna to the last antenna, then second Prbc for the 32
first to last antenna, and so on until reaching the last Prbc for the first to last antenna.  The bit-width per I and Q value is 33
variable (determined by M-Plane messaging) so after the very last Q value, some number of padding (set to zero) bits 34
may be inserted to get to the next byte boundary. When the optional “little endian byte order” is chosen via M-plane, the 35
ciIsample/ciQsample shall use little endian byte order to transmit the complex numbers. Refer to Annex D.1 for details.  36
Value range: {0000 0000 0000 0000b-1111 1111 1111 1111b} for each I and Q value 37
Type: signed integer. 38
Field length: variable bit-with per I and Q value. 39
 40

5.4.5.21 lbtMode (LBT Mode) 20
Description: Part of multi-carrier support. Indicates whether full LBT process is carried or partial LBT process is 21
carried (multi carrier mode B according to 3GPP TS 36.213 Section 15.1.5.2).  22
00b = full LBT (regular LBT, sending reservation signal until the beginning of the SF/slot) 23
01b = Partial LBT (looking back 25 sec prior to transmission as indicated in 3GPP TS 36.213 section 15.1.5.2) 24
10b = Partial LBT (looking back 34 sec prior to transmission as indicated in 3GPP TS 36.213 section 15.1.5.2) 25
11b = full LBT and stop (regular LBT, do NOT send reservation signal; O-RU senses the spectrum for the defer factor 26
+ a sensing slot right before OTA when the O-DU is ready to transmit data as indicated in 3GPP TS 36.213 27
section 15.1.1. i.e., right before the SF/slot boundary) 28
Value range: {00b - 11b} 29
Type: unsigned integer 30
Field length: 2 bits 31
 32
5.4.5.22 lbtPdschRes (LBT PDSCH Result) 33
Description: LBT result of SFN/SF 34
o 00b = not sensing – indicates that the O-RU is transmitting data 35
o 01b = currently sensing – indicates the O-RU has not yet acquired the channel 36
o 10b = success – indicates that the channel was successfully acquired 37
o 11b = Failure – indicates expiration of the LBT timer.  The LBT process should be reset. 38
Value range: {00b - 11b} 39
Type: unsigned integer 40
Field length: 1 bit 41

5.4.6.1 extType (extension type) 2
Description: This parameter provides the extension type which provides additional parameters specific to the subject 3
data extension.  An O-RU or O-DU receiving a “reserved” section extension shall ignore the extension and all 4
parameters contained within it. 5
Value range: {all zeros – all ones}.  See Table 5-14 for values. 6
Type: unsigned integer. 7
Field length: 7 bits. 8

5.4.6.2 ef (extension flag) 10
Description: This parameter is used to indicate if there is another extension present (ef=1) or this is the last extension 11
ef=0) 12
Value range: {0b=no more extensions; 1b=one or more extensions are included after this one}. 13
Type: binary bit. 14
Field length: 1 bit. 15
 16
5.4.6.3 extLen (extension length) 17
Description: This parameter provides the length of the section extension in units of 32-bit (or 4-byte) words.  The value 18
zero is reserved, so there is always at least one word in the extension (the word containing the extType a nd extLen). 19
Value range: {all zeros – all ones} – from one word to 255 words (8 bits) or 65535 words (16 bits). 20
Type: unsigned integer. 21
Field length: 8 bits (Section Extension =1 → =10) or 16 bits (Section Extension =11). 22

5.4.7 Coding of Information Elements – Application Layer, Section 24
Extensions 25
5.4.7.1 ExtType=1: Beamforming Weights Extension Type 26
This section applies to the sending of beamforming weights from the O-DU to the O-RU.  When this is done, the 27
weights are sent along with a beamID which is meant to allow those same weights to be used in future C -Plane 28
messages by invoking the same beamID (without the need to send the weights again).  This allows downloaded weights 29
to have “persistence” which should save DL throughput by not requiring sending of weights multiple times.  The K 30
parameter is defined in section 10.5.2.  Refer to Annex D for details the usual weight byte order.   The optional “little 31
endian byte order” is applied to bfwI/bfwQ fields if chosen via M-plane. Refer to Annex D.1 for details little endian 32
byte order. This section extension applies only to section types 1 and 3. 33

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2020 by the O-RAN Alliance.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        90
O-RAN.WG4.CUS.0-v03.00

5.4.7.2.8 zero-padding 7
Description: This parameter is intended to pad out the data to the next 4-byte boundary.  Because the preceding 8

5.4.7.3 ExtType=3: DL Precoding Extension Type 15
This section extension applies only to section types 1 and 3 and is to be used only for LTE TM2-4 not for other LTE 16
transmission modes and not for NR.  For other LTE transmission modes and for NR, precoding is assumed to be 17
included in the beamforming operation (that is, encoded in the beamforming weights) . 18
The following table shows the format of this section extension. 19
Table 5-22 : Extension Type 3 Data Format – first data layer 20
ef extType = 0x03 1 Octet N
extLen = 0x04 (4 words) 1 N+1
codebookIndex 1 N+2

crsReMask[7:0] 1 N+5

Table 5-23 : Extension Type 3 Data Format – not first data layer 22
ef extType = 0x03 1 Octet N
extLen = 0x01 (1 word) 1 N+1
codebookIndex 1 N+2
layerId ≠ 0000b or 1111b numLayers 1 N+3
 23
There may be two or four antenna ports hence two or four beamIDs needed (same beamID for user data and CRS REs).  24
For Antenna Port 0, the beamId is contained in the C-Plane data section header, while the Antenna Ports 1-3 beamIDs 25
are contained in this section extension.  When there are two antenna ports, the section extension only contains the 26
second Antenna Port beam ID (“beamIdAP1”) and the section extension length is 3 words (“extLen” = 0x 3).  When 27
there are four antenna ports, the section extension contains the second, third and fourth Antenna Port beam IDs 28
(“beamIdAP1”, “beamIdAP2”. And “beamIdAP3”) and the section extension length is 4 words (“extLen” = 0x 4). 29
For the txScheme indicating TxD, one Pcid is used for all the user data and one section instantiation is needed using the 30
corresponding C-Plane Rtcid, providing all the beam IDs (up to 4) for the user data; a second section instantiation  (same 31

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2020 by the O-RAN Alliance.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        95
O-RAN.WG4.CUS.0-v03.00
sectionId) with a different reMask may be used to provide the CRS RE beam IDs (also up to 4).   In the TxD case the 1
layerId is set to 1111b (“TxD”). 2
For the txSchemes indicating spatial multiplexing (LD CDD or no CDD), each layer will have its own Pcid for the user 3
data with a corresponding C-Plane Rtcid conveying the user data’s beamId, with this section extension showing a 4
different layer number for each layer.  Only within the layer ID zero Rtcid will the CRS REs be provided with their 5
beamIDs (one beamId in the section header and the other beamIDs in this section extension) . For the non-zero layer 6
number Rtcids, this section extension will still be provided to guide the precoding operation (provide the layer ID) but 7
will not include beamIds (extLen = 0x1), and the beamId in the section header should be ignored by the O-RU and 8
should be set to the default value by the O-DU. 9

5.4.7.5.1 mcScaleReMask  (modulation compression power scale RE mask) 3
Description: This parameter defines the Resource Element (RE) mask to indicate the position of RE with same scaling 4
and modulation type within a PRB. Each bit setting in the mcScaleReMask indicates if the mcScaleOffset and csf fields 5
are applicable to the RE sent in U-Plane messages or not (0=not applicable; 1=applicable).  MSB indicates the value for 6
the RE of the lowest frequency in a PRB. 7
Note that different REs in a PRB may be indicated by different invocations of mcScaleReMask within extension field 8
type 5.  If any RE in a PRB is never pointed to by a mcScaleReMask (but other REs in that PRB are), the “missing” RE 9
should be considered to represent not populated REs (e.g. no user data to transmit). 10
There is a relationship between the mcScaleReMask values and the section’s reMask: no bit in any of the 11
mcScaleReMasks should be set (=1) in a position where the reMask has a zero, and every reMask bit that is set (=1) 12
should have exactly one bit =1 in one of the mcScaleReMasks.  If these rules are violated, the O-RU’s reaction is 13
undefined.  14
Value range: {0000 0000 0000b-1111 1111 1111b}. 15

5.4.7.6 ExtType=6: Non-contiguous PRB allocation in time and frequency domain 3
This section extension applies only to Section Types 1, 3 and 5. 4
This section extension enables allocation of non-contiguous sets of PRBs (Resource Block Groups, or RBGs) in 5
frequency and time domain. This will reduce significantly the C-Plane overhead when users or channels are allocated 6
with non-contiguous sets of PRBs in time and frequency. 7
If this section extension is present in a section description then the field startSymbolId in the message header and the 8
fields rb, symInc, and numSymbol in the section description are not used for identification of symbols and PRBs 9
referred by the section description (the values of these parameters can be used by other section descriptions in the 10
message; note sender may set symInc and numSymbol to any allowed value without restriction to values corresponding 11
to symbols actually referred by the section description with Section Extension =6).  Sender shall set rb to the value of 12
zero. Sender shall set startSymbolId to the earliest symbol referred by any of section descriptions in the message, 13
including, but not limited to, section descriptions with Section Extension =6. The earliest symbol referenced by a 14
section description with Section Extension =6 is the earliest symbol selected by a set bit in the symbolMask. That 15
means symbolMask’s bit n, such that n < startSymbolId, must be zero. 16
Usage of this section extension does not affect the operation of user plane. It is noted that a data section in the user 17
plane is not required to contain a contiguous range of PRBs. By invoking the sectionId multiple times in the user plane, 18
either within a single message or in different messages, sets of non-contiguous PRBs can be handled. 19
Note that utilization of the non-contiguous PRB allocation section extension does not put any restriction on utilization 20
of sections with contiguous PRB utilization except for the general rules of utilization of sections e.g. a resource element 21
must have one and only one referred section (identified by sectionId) in the control plane. 22
In case a control plane section is cited multiple times then all citations shall allocate same set of PRBs an d symbols. 23
Note that when utilizing this section extension together with Section Type 3 where freqOffset parameter is present, then 24
freqOffset affects the frequency span for the specific range of PRB numbers. 25
 26
Table 5-28: Section Format for Section Extension 6 (non-contiguous PRB allocation in time and frequency) 27
ef extType = 0x06 1 Octet N
extLen 0x02 (2 words) 1 N+1
res rbgSize [2:0] rbgMask [27:24] 1 N+2
rbgMask [23:16] 1 N+3
rbgMask[15:8] 1 N+4
rbgMask[7:0] 1 N+5
reserved symbolMask[13:8] 1 N+6
symbolMask[7:0] 1 N+7
 28
 29
5.4.7.6.1 rbgSize (resource block group size) 30
Description: This parameter indicates the size in number of PRBs of the resource block groups allocated by the bit 31
mask. The size of the resource block group to be used by the application shall be taken from the mapping table given in 32
the Value range field in the rbgMask description below. See rbgMask for special handling of exceptional resource block 33
groups. 34
Value range: {000b: reserved, 001b: 1, 010b: 2, 011b: 3, 100b: 4, 101b: 6, 110b: 8, 111b: 16}. 35
Type: unsigned integer. 36
Field length: 3 bits. 37
Default Value: 001b. 38

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2020 by the O-RAN Alliance.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        101
O-RAN.WG4.CUS.0-v03.00
 1
5.4.7.6.2 rbgMask (resource block group bit mask) 2
Description: This parameter is a bit mask where each bit indicates whether a corresponding resource block group is 3
allocated. If bit n in the mask is set, then the resource block group n is allocated where  n can take values in range [0, 4
lastRbgid] where  5
lastRbgid = ceiling( (numPrbc + (startPrbc mod rbgSize))/ rbgSize ) - 1. 6
The range of PRBs included in a resource block group is given as follows 7
Resource block group 0 include PRBs with id in the range [startPrbc, startPrbc+f(0)-1]. 8
Resource block group n include PRBs with id in the range [startPrbc + f(0) + (n -1)*f(n), startPrbc + f(0) + n*f(n)-1] 9
where 0 < n < lastRbgid. 10
Resource block group n = lastRbgid include PRBs with id in the range [startPrbc + numPrbc – f(lastRbgid), startPrbc+ 11
numPrbc -1]. 12
Where f(n) gives the number of PRBs included in resource block group n is given as follows:  13
f(0) = rbgSize – (startPrbc mod rbgSize) 14
f(n) = rbgSize, where 0<n<lastRbgid. 15
if (startPrbc + numPrbc) mod rbgsize > 0 then  f(lastRbgid) = (startPrbc + numPrbc) mod rbgSize 16
else  f(lastRbgid) = rbgSize 17
Only PRBs within the range defined by startPrbc and numPrbc can be allocated ie [startPrbc, numPrbc -1]. In case 18
numPrbc is zero the PRB range is all PRBs as defined by the eAxC and startPrbc shall be set to zero. Transmitter shall 19
ensure that rbgMask does not have non-zero bits outside the valid range [0, lastRbgid], if receiver detects non-zero bits 20
outside the valid range, those shall be ignored. 21
Transmitter shall ensure that combinations of startPrbc, numPrbc and rbgSize leading to a value of lastRbgid larger than 22
27 (number of bits available in the rbgMask field - 1) are never used. Such combinations are invalid and if detected by 23
the receiver the section shall be ignored. 24
MSB of rbgMask indicates the highest-frequency resource block group. 25
 26
Value range: {0000 0000 0000 0000 0000 0000 0000b - 1111 1111 1111 1111 1111 1111 1111b}. 27
Type: unsigned integer (bit mask). 28
Field length: 28 bits. 29
Default Value: 1111 1111 1111 1111 1111 1111 1111b (all resource block groups allocated). 30
 31
 32
Figure 5-8 Resource block group definition example. 33
 34
5.4.7.6.3 symbolMask (symbol bit mask) 35
Description: This parameter is a bit mask where each bit indicates whether the rbgMask applies to a given symbol in 36
the slot.    If bit n is set then the rbgMask is applied to symbol n, where n has range [0..13].  If no bits are set this 37
implies the rbgMask may be applied to no RBGs in the slot, in other words there are no RE allocations in the slot (or a 38

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2020 by the O-RAN Alliance.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        102
O-RAN.WG4.CUS.0-v03.00
different data section contains the RE allocation for the slot).  If the symbolMask values indicate allocations beyond a 1
slot boundary, such allocations shall be ignored (e.g. when there are fewer than 14 symbols in a slot).  2
LSB of symbolMask indicates symbol zero (the first symbol to arrive in a slot). 3
Value range: {00 0000 0000 0000b-11 1111 1111 1111b}. 4
Type: unsigned integer (bit mask). 5
Field length: 14 bits. 6
Default Value: 11 1111 1111 1111b (section repeated in 14 symbols). 7

5.4.7.7 ExtType=7: eAxC Mask Section Extension 9
This section extension is meant to allow a specific C-Plane message to apply not to just a single c_eAxC value but to 10
multiple c_eAxC values.  The intended use case applies to Section Type 0, wherein the intention is to allow blanking 11
(designated by Section Type 0) to be indicated for multiple c_eAxC values e.g. all component carriers.   Table 5-29 12
shows the section extension format. 13
Table 5-29 : Section Format for Section Extension 6 (eAxC Mask parameter) 14
ef extType = 0x07 1 Octet N
extLen = 0x01 (1 word) 1 N+1
eAxCmask[15:8] 1 N+2
eAxCmask[7:0] 1 N+3
 15
When a C-Plane message with this Section Extension is received by an O-RU, the O-RU should react as if multiple C-16
Plane messages were received with all of the c_eAxC values permitted by the mask.   Note that using the mask, it is 17
possible the O-RU may assume the C-Plane message content applies to c_eAxC values that are not intended and are not 18
used (e.g. if two bits of the mask are set to zero to indicate the message applies to all 3 sectors, there will be a non -19
existent fourth sector that will be implied too).  In this case there will be no U -Plane data specified for the spurious 20
c_eAxC value(s) and the O-RU should not consider this as an error. 21
Support of this Section Extension is optional: if an O-RU reports a capability excluding support of this Section 22
Extension then the O-DU must not employ it, and if the O-DU does not support this section extension the same effect 23
can be obtained using multiple single-c_eAxC C-Plane messages so no functionality is lost (though the C-Plane will be 24
less efficient).  25
5.4.7.7.1 eAxCmask (eAxC Mask) 26
Description: This binary mask indicates which c_eAxC values the C-Plane message applies to.  A “0” bit in the mask 27
means the specified c_eAxC bit is “don’t care” while a “1” bit in the mask means the specified c_eAxC bit should be 28
considered.  An all-zero eAxCmask means “use this message for all c_eAxC values” while an all-ones eAxCmask 29
means “use this message for only the designated c_eAxC value”.  In the former case (“use this message for all c_eAxC 30
values”), the actual c_eAxC value in the C-Plane message header could be any value because the message would apply 31
to all c_eAxC values regardless of the actual value in the C-Plane message.  In the latter case (“use this message for 32
only the designated c_eAxC value”) this section extension adds no value because that is the normal operation.  33
The intended use of the mask is to indicate which sub-field of the c_eAxC the message applies to.  For example, if a 34
single sector single band of the O-RU will be blanked for all component carriers, the RU-Port-ID and CC-ID sub-field 35
portions of the eAxCmask would be all zeros (“use this message for all layers/spatial streams and all component 36
carriers”) while the other subfield portions of the eAxCmask would be all ones (“use this message for the specific band, 37
sector, and DU_Port_ID values provided in the c_eAxC”).  In this way a Section Type 0 message could indicate the 38
blanking of all component-carriers in a band-sector in a single C-Plane message. 39
Value range: {0000 0000 0000 0000b-1111 1111 1111 1111b}. 40
Type: unsigned integer (bit mask). 41
Field length: 16 bits. 42
Default Value: 1111 1111 1111 1111b (all bits of c_eAxC are considered). 43

Copyright © 2020 by the O-RAN Alliance.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        103
O-RAN.WG4.CUS.0-v03.00

5.4.7.8 ExtType=8: Regularization factor 2
This section extension is for regularizationFactor which is used to generate MU beamforming weight for the scheduled 3
UEs in a slot. regularizationFactor is the noise variance used for MMSE (Minimum Mean Square Error) computation of 4
generating MU BFW. The intended use case applies to Section Type 5 for sending regularization factor instead of 5
sending regularization factor over Section Type 6. 6
Support of this Section Extension is mandatory for O-RUs supporting Section Type 5 in this version of the 7
specification. If an O-RU reports a capability excluding support of this Section Extension (O-RUs supporting previous 8
version of specification or O-RUs not supporting Section Type 5), then the O-DU must not employ it, and if the O-RU 9
reports a capability including support of this section extension then O-DU supporting this version of specification must 10
employ this section extension instead Section Type 6 to convey regularization factor.  11
See Annex J for further description of the regularization factor’s use in UL and DL. 12

5.4.7.10 ExtType=10: Section description for group configuration of multiple ports 11
This section extension applies to section types 1, 3 and 5. C-plane section information for the multiple ports (i.e., layers 12
or Tx/Rx paths) may be the same except beam IDs or UE IDs in most cell scheduling case. When the multiple ports 13
share the common section information within O-RU, C-plane sections to be sent via the corresponding ports are merged 14
into a C-plane section via a specified port using this section extension. M-plane pre-configures to group the ports to be 15
merged and to specify the port to represent them. The beam ID in the section of the representative port can be 16
considered an index which indicates a set of multiple beam vectors (beam IDs) each of which applies to the 17
corresponding port (layer or Tx/Rx path). 18

5.5.3 C-Plane Optimization using Section Extension =10 10
In general, the O-DU uses unique eAxC ids to address each layer or spatial stream when sending C -plane and U-plane 11
messages to the O-RU. In many situations, information contained in C-plane messages for the different spatial streams 12
is the same or similar. For example, a SU MIMO allocation with 8 layers may have same values for startPrbc, 13
NumPrbc, reMask, and numSymbol in the section header for all 8 C-plane messages, one message per layer. In this 14
case, Section Extension =10 can be used along with a ‘representative eAxC’ ID (M-plane configured) to reduce C-plane 15
overhead of sending multiple messages to the overhead of sending one single C -plane message. This is an optional 16
feature which be taken advantage of by the O-DU if the O-RU capability indicates that the O-RU supports Section 17
Extension =10. Based on this capability, the O-RU can be configured with a ‘representative eAxC’ ID representing all 8 18
eAxC IDs in above example. Once a ‘representative eAxC’ id is configured, the O-DU can send one single C-plane 19
message addressed to the ‘representative eAxC’ ID along with the Section Extension Type 10 instead of 8 C -plane 20
messages in above example case. Once the O-RU receives a C-plane message addressed to the ‘representative eAxC’ ID 21
and with Section Extension Type 10, then the O-RU applies this message to all endpoints pointed to by the 22
‘representative eAxC’ ID whereby performing same operation just like it had received 8 different C -plane messages. 23
Figure 5-9 below illustrates the example.    24
 25
 26
Figure 5-9 : Operation of Section Extension =10 27

5.5.4 C-Plane Optimization using Section Extension =11 29
Section Extension =11 referes to flexible beamforming weight transmission.  One way to transfer per -PRB 30
beamforming weights is using Section Extension =1 and creating one section for each PRB. This introduces high 31
overhead in the form of section headers and section extensions. The objective of Section Extension =11 is to eliminate 32
this problem by allowing the inclusion of the beamforming weights for multiple PRBs i n a single section. 33
Example use case include zero-forcing beamforming (or similar methods) by using per-PRB channel information to 34
calculate per-PRB beamforming weights. Specifically, the O-RU sends UL pilots (SRS) to O-DU, which in return 35
calculates per-PRB beamforming weights in the O-DU, then transfer them to the O-RU. These weights can be updated 36
every slot, as an example.  37

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2020 by the O-RAN Alliance.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        109
O-RAN.WG4.CUS.0-v03.00
Section Extension =11 gives the flexibility of either sending the sets of beamforming weights along with the section 1
extension beamIds, or only the section extension beamIds (after, obviously, loading the beamforming weights in a 2
previous time).  3
Notes: 4
1. By default, the section beamID will have no meaning if used with section extension 10 and will be neglected 5
by the O-RU 6
2. The O-DU must set the section beamID = 0x7FFF, which means that the O-RU should ignore it. 7

5.5.4.1 Interaction between Section Extension =11 and Section Extension =6 9
Section Extension =6 is used for non-contiguous PRB allocation in both time and frequency domains. The  main 10
parameter in Section Extension =6 that is used to identify the PRB groups is rbgSize. On the other hand, numBundPrb 11
is used in Section Extension =11 to identify the number of bundled PRBs that share the same beamforming weights 12
vector for L TRXs. Both section extensions can be used together, however, few rules need to be followed:  13
First case: RAD = 1 14
1) In principle, numBundPrb may not be the same as rbgSize 15
2) For each contiguous set of PRBs as defined under Section Extension =6 (if used), the O-RU starts counting for 16
the number of bundled PRBs and applying the sets of beamforming weights to PRB bundles in an increasing 17
order of PRBs 18
a. If the last bundled PRB doesn’t coincide with the last RBG in the contiguous set of PRBs, then the 19
unassigned PRBs (i.e., PRBs with unassigned beamforming weights) will be considered orphan 20
PRB(s) 21
3) Orphan PRBs are allocated the following set of beamforming weights (i.e., set after the  last set that was 22
assigned to a regular PRB bundle) although the number of PRBs is less than a PRB bundleFor any set of PRBs 23
that are not being assigned using Section Extension =6, no beamforming weight sets are assigned 24
4) For the following set of contiguous PRBs allocated in the same symbol after the discontinuity, the O-RU will 25
apply the following set of beamforming weights (starting from the last set of beamforming weights allocated to the 26
last PRB bundle in the previous contiguous PRB set). 27
5) The process continues until all the PRBs defined under Section Extension =6 are assigned beamforming weights. 28
At this point, all the sets of beamforming weights under Section Extension =10 should have been assigned.  29
6) Based on the symbol mask, the O-RU applies the same sets of beamforming weights to the corresponding PRB 30
bundles similar to the first assigned symbol. 31
 32
Example 1: RAD = 1b (see Figure 5-10 below) 33
symbolMask = 10 0001 0001 0000b 34
rbgSize = 3 35
numBundPRB = 2 36
Total number of L beamforming weights set = 7 37

Chapter 6 U-plane Protocol 1
6.1 General 2
6.1.1 U-plane Transport 3
Either eCPRI or IEEE 1914.3 is used as an encapsulation mechanism for the user-plane messages. Due to the nature of 4
these messages (very strict delay constraints), it is assumed that message acknowledgements are not possible. Likewise, 5
different data flows may be used for the User-Plane and Control-Plane messages.  6
6.1.2 U-plane Data Compression 7
U-Plane IQ data, (both DL and UL) including user data, PRACH and control channels may be transmitted in 8
compressed format. There are several envisioned compression methods including an “uncompressed” format. The 9
method of compression is variable based on sectionId but is constant for every section in a single C -Plane message.  10
Likewise, the I and Q bitwidth of the compressed samples is variable based on sectionId but is constant for every 11
section in a single C-Plane message.  The block compression methods are performed on Physical Resource Block 12
(PRB) basis (i.e. 12 x Resource Elements per PRB).  More specific details on the supported compression methods may 13
be found in Annex A. 14
An optional capability configures static IQ format and compression method, in which case the M-Plane defines the 15
static IQ format (bitwidth) and compression method.  In this case there are four fewer bytes in the U -Plane section 16
header, at the cost of less flexibility.  For static IQ data format and compression method, there are actually four sets of 17
data formats and compression methods: for LTE DL, LTE UL, NR DL and NR UL.  This allows the taking advantage 18
of the static format while still allowing some compression flexibility e.g. allowing modulation compression on the DL 19
(which only applies to DL) and some other compression method on the UL 20
6.1.3 Digital Power Scaling 21
6.1.3.1 Definition of IQ Power in dBFS 22
IQ power level in dBFS (dB full scale) is a logarithmic representation of the power level for an IQ sample carried over 23
the digital interface. IQ power level in dBFS is proportional to logarithm of I²+Q²: 24
IQ power level [dBFS] = 10·log10( I²+Q² ) - 10·log10(FS) 25
where FS = max(I²) = max(Q²) = max(I²+Q²) with max over all IQ values that can be represented by interface 26
For frequency domain IQ data, 0 dBFS is the maximum power level which can be carried by one subcarrier . The 27
smallest non-zero IQ power level is defined by the interface resolution.  28
It is expected that an O-RU will normalize any received DL value to its internal representation of full scale so that a 0 29
dBFS can be properly handled. 30
Example: 31
I=min I, Q=0 32
With 9bit mantissa 2’s complement + 4bit exponent compression:  min I = -256·2^15 = -2^23 →  33
0 dBFS  average(I²+Q²) = 2^46 34
Interface resolution  1/2^46  -138.47dBFs 35
6.1.3.2 Definition of Gain over Fronthaul Interface 36
The gain of an array defines the relation between the levels of a test signal seen at its input and output, also called 37
digital power scaling. The gain of an array can be calculated from the gain of one element of the array while assuming 38
all elements have same gain. Figure 6-1 depicts the gain relations between the digital interface and the RF reference 39
plane to an assumed lossless antenna (i.e., antenna insertion losses are counted as part of the gain in both DL and UL 40
direction).  41

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2020 by the O-RAN Alliance.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        113
O-RAN.WG4.CUS.0-v03.00
 1
Figure 6-1 : DL and UL Gain over fronthaul interface 2
Both DL and UL gains in [dB] are described by the following relations 3
DL gain [dB] = RF output level [dBm] – IQ input level [dBFS]  4
UL gain [dB] = IQ output level [dBFS] – RF input level [dBm]  5
Where: 6
‘RF output level [dBm]’ and ‘RF input level [dBm]’ are RF signal level in dBm at reference plane to an assumed 7
lossless antenna when the antenna is integrated inside the O-RU, or at TAB connector if antenna is not integrated inside 8
the O-RU. The rms output power [dBm] is measured per array element as Total Radiated Power TRP (i.e., excluding 9
any antenna directivity gain). The rms input power [dBm] is measured per array element after including the antenna 10
directivity gain. Note that the antenna directivity gain resuts from the array element directivity + 10·log10(number of 11
elements). Hence, when evaluating the array element gain, the antenna directivity is reduced to the array element 12
directivity. 13
‘IQ input level [dBFS]’ and ‘IQ output level [dBFS]’ are 10·log10(average(I²+Q²)) normalized such that 0dBFS is the 14
maximum nominal (r.m.s.) power level which can be achieved with a constant IQ signal with arbitrary phase (i.e., for 15
frequency-domain IQ signal for one sub-carrier, constant over time). 16
In O-RUs supporting beamforming, the actual DL gain and UL gain of the array element can be impacted by the gain 17
level of beam weight used and which can change dynamically during operation. Such dependency on the beam 18
pattern shall be excluded when describing any configurable gain or reported gain (as O-RU capability).  19
For an exact definition of DL and UL gain, the respective input test signals need to be declared by the O-RU vendor; 20
this is not in scope of this specification. [For information only: This can be e.g., CW signal at carrier center or test 21
signals/reference signals defined by 3GPP; for DL gain those being defined to test accuracy of the maximum output 22
power (3GPP TS36.141 section 6.2→ 38.141) and for UL gain those being defined to test absolute accuracy of 23
Received Interference Power (3GPP TS 36.133 section 10.1.1 → 38.133)].  In Figure 6-2 the details of DL gain are 24
described. For every tx-array, O-RU reports (as capability) the maximal configurable DL gain of one element of the 25
array (alternatively the nominal power per tx-array element mapped to 0dBFS). In addition, the O-DU configures over 26
the M-Plane the DL gain to be used per tx-array element for a certain carrier configuration. 27
The values for the max configurable DL gain and configured DL gain assume: 28
• No power loss/gain due to beamforming weights;  29
• all available DL power can be allocated to one array carrier in a single eAxC; 30
 31
O-RU
digital input to O-RU: IQ power
levels are measured in dBFS

Figure 6-2 : Details of DL Gain 2
In Figure 6-3 the details of UL gain are described. For every rx-array, O-RU reports (as capability) an UL 3
gain_correction_range in dB of one element of the array (applicable to all the elements of the array). The 4
gain_correction_range is signed, has a max and min value, and a step size. It shall be allowed to report at least a range 5
of ±20dB and a resolution of 0.01dB. In addition, the O-DU configures over the M-Plane a gain_correction value to be 6
used per rx-array element for a certain carrier configuration. The O-RU can then configure its internal UL gain of the 7
rx-array element for that carrier (rx-array carrier element) if the IQ compression method is configured as static. In case 8
the compression method is dynamic, the internal gain of the O-RU will be dynamic and depending on compression 9
information received in realtime over the C-Plane.  10

• No power loss/gain due to beeamforming weights. 12
